Aesthetics â€“ Talks about beauty, art, and why we like certain things.

Political Philosophy â€“ Looks at laws, rights, freedom, and what makes a fair society or government.

Philosophy of Mind â€“ Tries to understand thoughts, feelings, and how the mind works.

Philosophy of Science â€“ Studies how science works, what it can prove, and what its limits are.

5/11/25, 3:13â€¯PM - Hassan Ahmad Cs Kust: *Explanation and Answer to the Questions:*

*Question 1: UML Diagram for Construction Materials Management System*
You are tasked with designing a *Construction Materials Management System*. Let's break this down into manageable pieces.

*a) UML Class Diagram:*

We will have several classes:

1. *Material* (Base Class)
   - Attributes: name, quantity, unitPrice, purchaseDate, totalCost
   - Methods: `calculate_total_cost()`, `display_material_summary()`

2. *RawMaterial* (Subclass of Material)
   - Attributes: supplierName, supplierAddress, supplierContact
   - Methods: `display_supplier_details()`

3. *FinishingMaterial* (Subclass of Material)
   - Attributes: manufacturerName, manufacturerContact
   - Methods: `display_manufacturer_details()`

4. *Furniture* (Subclass of FinishingMaterial)
   - Attributes: locationInHouse
   - Methods: `display_furniture_details()`

5. *Supplier* (Class for managing suppliers)
   - Attributes: supplierName, supplierAddress, supplierContact
   - Methods: `get_supplier_info()`

6. *Builder* (Class for managing builder information)
   - Attributes: builderName, builderAddress, builderContact, constructionSite
   - Methods: `get_builder_info()`

The relationships:
5/11/25, 3:13â€¯PM - Hassan Ahmad Cs Kust: - *Material* is the parent class, and *RawMaterial* and *FinishingMaterial* are child classes.
- *FinishingMaterial* has further subclasses, like *Furniture*.
- *RawMaterial* and *FinishingMaterial* both depend on *Supplier* and *Builder* classes for their respective data.

*b) Relationship Explanation:*
- *Inheritance*: RawMaterial and FinishingMaterial inherit from Material because they share some common attributes like name, quantity, unit price, etc.
- *Association*: Material has an association with *Supplier* (for raw materials) and *Builder* (for builder information) because raw materials are sourced from suppliers, and the builder manages the construction site.
- *Aggregation*: The *Furniture* class is an aggregation of *FinishingMaterial* because furniture is a specific type of finishing material.

---

*Question 2: Furniture Class Implementation*

```python
class Furniture:
    def _init_(self, color, price, location):
        self.color = color
        self.price = price
        self.location = location

Example usage
furniture = Furniture("Red", 1500, "Living Room")
print(furniture.color, furniture.price, furniture.location)
```

*Explanation*:
5/11/25, 3:13â€¯PM - Hassan Ahmad Cs Kust: - *`_init_` method* is the constructor. It initializes the *color*, *price*, and *location* attributes of the Furniture object when an instance is created.

---

*Question 3: `str` Method for the Furniture Class*

```python
class Furniture:
    def _init_(self, color, price, location):
        self.color = color
        self.price = price
        self.location = location
    
    def _str_(self):
        return f"Furniture Details: \nColor: {self.color}\nPrice: {self.price}\nLocation: {self.location}"

Example usage
furniture = Furniture("Red", 1500, "Living Room")
print(furniture)
```

*Explanation*:
- The *`_str_` method* is a special method in Python. It allows us to define how the object is represented as a string. Here, we format the output neatly to display the furniture's details in a structured way when the object is printed.

---

*Question 4: Object Instantiation and Input Handling*

```python
class Furniture:
    def _init_(self, color, price, location):
        self.color = color
        self.price = price
        self.location = location
    
    def set_color(self, color):
        self.color = color
    
    def set_price(self, price):
        self.price = price
    
    def display_price_location(self):
5/11/25, 3:13â€¯PM - Hassan Ahmad Cs Kust: return f"Price: {self.price}, Location: {self.location}"

a) Instantiating the object
furniture = Furniture("Red", 1500, "Living Room")

b) Taking input from user to update values
furniture.set_color(input("Enter the new color: "))
furniture.set_price(float(input("Enter the new price: ")))

c) Display the updated price and location
print(furniture.display_price_location())
```

*Explanation*:
- *Instantiating the object*: We create an instance of the `Furniture` class with initial values ("Red", 1500, "Living Room").
- *Updating color and price*: We use the setter methods `set_color` and `set_price` to change the color and price of the furniture.
- *Displaying price and location*: We display the updated price and location by calling the `display_price_location` method.

---

*Tips for Solving Similar Questions*:

1. *Understand the Problem Statement*:
   - Break the problem into parts. What are the main classes? What attributes and methods do they need? What relationships exist between the classes?

2. *Use OOP Concepts*:
   - Classes and objects: Identify which parts of the system can be objects (e.g., `Furniture`, `RawMaterial`, `Supplier`).
5/11/25, 3:13â€¯PM - Hassan Ahmad Cs Kust: - Inheritance: If classes share common behavior, think of using inheritance. For example, `RawMaterial` and `FinishingMaterial` can inherit from a base class `Material`.
   - Encapsulation: Keep the data hidden using private attributes and provide methods to access or update them.

3. *Flow*:
   - First, create the class and define the constructor (`_init_`).
   - Define the required methods such as setters/getters or display methods.
   - Identify the relationships between classes and use inheritance or composition accordingly.
   - Test the code by creating objects and calling their methods to ensure that everything works as expected.

4. *Practice*:
   - Work on similar problems to get better at identifying which OOP concept to apply and how to implement it.
   - Write small pieces of code, and gradually build up the complexity. For example, first, try creating a class with just an `_init_` constructor and then add more methods incrementally.
  
By following this approach, you can manage large questions systematically and tackle OOP-based problems with confidence. Good luck with your paper!

5/12/25, 10:23â€¯PM - Salman Kust Cs: *Integrated Circuits (ICs)*

Imagine you have a lot of LEGO blocks, and each block can do a specific job. Now, imagine someone took all these LEGO blocks and glued them together into a single, small piece. That's kind of like an Integrated Circuit, or IC.

What is an IC?
An IC is a tiny piece of electronics that has many small parts inside it. These parts work together to do a specific job.

How Does it Work?
Think of an IC like a tiny factory. Each part inside the IC does a specific job, like sorting, counting, or sending signals. When you give the IC some power and tell it what to do, it starts working like a tiny machine.

Types of ICs
1. *Memory ICs*: These ICs help store information, like your favorite games or pictures.
2. *Processor ICs*: These ICs are like the brain of a computer. They help make decisions and do calculations.
3. *Amplifier ICs*: These ICs help make weak signals stronger.

Why are ICs Important?
1. *Small Size*: ICs are very small, which makes them perfect for tiny devices like smartphones.
2. *Fast and Efficient*: ICs can process information very quickly and use less power.
3. *Reliable*: ICs are designed to work correctly and reliably.

Examples of ICs
1. *Smartphones*: ICs help your phone work, like processing information and sending signals.
2. *Computers*: ICs are used in computers to process information and store data.
3. *Gaming Consoles*: ICs help make games run smoothly and look great.

ICs are like tiny superheroes that help make our devices work!

5/14/25, 10:40â€¯AM - M. Waqas Cs Kust: Here are three descriptive paragraphsâ€”one each on Online Learning, Classroom Learning, and University Life:


---

1. Online Learning:
Online learning is a modern method of education that allows students to attend classes via the internet. It offers great flexibility, enabling learners to study from anywhere at their own pace. Virtual platforms like Zoom, Google Meet, and learning management systems provide lectures, assignments, and discussion forums. While it saves time and travel costs, online learning requires self-discipline and a stable internet connection. It has become especially popular during times when in-person classes are not possible, such as during the COVID-19 pandemic.


---

2. Classroom Learning:
Classroom learning is the traditional way of education where students and teachers interact face-to-face. This setting creates a structured environment where students can ask questions, participate in group discussions, and receive instant feedback. The classroom also helps in developing social skills, teamwork, and discipline. It fosters a sense of community and motivation among learners. Despite technological advancements, many people still consider classroom learning more effective for understanding complex concepts.


---

3. University Life:
University life is a significant and memorable phase in a student's journey. It is not only about academic growth but also about personal development and independence. Students experience a new level of freedom and responsibility, meet people from diverse backgrounds, and participate in various extracurricular activities. The university environment encourages critical thinking, research, and creativity. It is a time for building oneâ€™s future career while enjoying social events, friendships, and self-discovery.

5/20/25, 1:06â€¯PM - Salman Kust Cs: Here is a list of common vocabulary used in academic writing, grouped by purpose:


---

1. Introducing Ideas

According to

It is widely believed that

Research suggests

The purpose of this study is to



---

2. Adding Information

Furthermore

Moreover

In addition

Similarly



---

3. Contrasting Ideas

However

On the other hand

Although

Despite

In contrast



---

4. Giving Examples

For instance

For example

Such as

To illustrate



---

5. Showing Cause and Effect

Therefore

As a result

Consequently

Thus

Due to



---

6. Concluding

In conclusion

To summarize

Overall

In brief



---

7. Describing Research

This study examinesâ€¦

The data indicatesâ€¦

Findings revealâ€¦

The evidence supportsâ€¦



---

Would you like a printable version or examples using these in full sentences?
5/20/25, 1:06â€¯PM - Salman Kust Cs: Hereâ€™s a printable-style academic vocabulary list with example sentences:


---

1. Introducing Ideas

According to Smith (2020), climate change is accelerating.

It is widely believed that exercise improves mental health.

Research suggests that sleep affects academic performance.

The purpose of this study is to explore student motivation.



---

2. Adding Information

Furthermore, regular reading improves vocabulary.

Moreover, it enhances critical thinking skills.

In addition, it builds concentration.

Similarly, writing also improves cognitive ability.



---

3. Contrasting Ideas

However, not all students benefit equally.

On the other hand, some studies show no clear connection.

Although the method is effective, it is time-consuming.

Despite the benefits, few use it regularly.

In contrast, online learning is more flexible.



---

4. Giving Examples

For instance, many students use flashcards to memorize terms.

For example, social media platforms help in language learning.

Tools such as Grammarly support writing improvement.

To illustrate, a case study was conducted at a local university.



---

5. Showing Cause and Effect

The data was incomplete; therefore, the results are limited.

As a result, the hypothesis was not confirmed.

Funding was cut; consequently, the project ended early.

Thus, further research is needed.

The delay was due to technical issues.



---

6. Concluding

In conclusion, early preparation leads to better results.

To summarize, the findings support the theory.

Overall, students showed improved understanding.

In brief, the project met its goals.



---

7. Describing Research

This study examines the impact of diet on memory.

The data indicates a positive correlation.

Findings reveal a significant improvement.

The evidence supports the use of technology in classrooms.



---

*Explanation (Points):*

6/25/25, 10:34â€¯AM - Iftikhar Kust Cs Fr: class Doctor:
    def __init__(self, idNo, name, specialization, contact_no, email):
        self.__idNo = idNo
        self.__name = name
        self.__specialization = specialization
        self.__contact_no = contact_no
        self.__email = email

    def get_idNo(self):
        return self.__idNo

    def get_name(self):
        return self.__name


class Patient:
    def __init__(self, patientID, name, disease, contact_no, appointmentDate):
        self.__patientID = patientID
        self.__name = name
        self.__disease = disease
        self.__contact_no = contact_no
        self.__appointmentDate = appointmentDate

    def set_name(self, name):
        self.__name = name

    def set_contact_no(self, contact_no):
        self.__contact_no = contact_no

    def get_id(self):
        return self.__patientID


class Receptionist:
    def __init__(self, idNo, name, birthdate, hiredate):
        self.__idNo = idNo
        self.__name = name
        self.__birthdate = birthdate
        self.__hiredate = hiredate


class CheckUp:
    def __init__(self, checkupID, date_checkup, follow_up_date, disease, doctor, patient):
        self.__checkupID = checkupID
        self.__date_checkup = date_checkup
        self.__follow_up_date = follow_up_date
        self.__disease = disease
        self.__doctor = doctor
        self.__patient = patient

    def __str__(self):
        return (f"Checkup ID: {self.__checkupID}\n"
                f"Date: {self.__date_checkup}\n"
                f"Follow-up: {self.__follow_up_date}\n"
                f"Disease: {self.__disease}\n"
                f"Doctor: {self.__doctor.get_name()} (ID: {self.__doctor.get_idNo()})\n"
                f"Patient ID: {self.__patient.get_id()}")

7/9/25, 12:16â€¯PM - Muhaib Fr: Apky Sath notes ha
7/9/25, 12:20â€¯PM - +92 325 8617855: Small-Scale Integration (SSI):
SSI circuits contain a small number of components, typically ranging from a few to around 100 transistors or logic gates. Examples include basic logic gates like AND, OR, and NOT gates. 
Medium-Scale Integration (MSI):
MSI circuits integrate a larger number of components, typically between 100 and a few thousand transistors or logic gates. Examples include counters, registers, and decoders. 
Large-Scale Integration (LSI):
LSI circuits incorporate a significantly larger number of components, ranging from a few thousand to tens of thousands of transistors or logic gates. Examples include microprocessors and memory chips. 
Very Large-Scale Integration (VLSI):
VLSI circuits contain hundreds of thousands to millions of transistors or logic gates. Modern CPUs and complex memory chips fall under this category. 
Ultra Large-Scale Integration (ULSI):
ULSI circuits are the most complex, integrating millions to billions of transistors or logic gates. Modern microprocessors and large memory devices utilize ULSI technology.

10/8/25, 5:12â€¯PM - M. Waqas Cs Kust: How to check aggregate? Ply anyone reply
10/8/25, 5:14â€¯PM - Salman Kust Cs: *Aggregate check karne ke liye:*

- *Aggregate marks* = (Total marks obtained in all subjects / Total marks of all subjects) * 100

*Ya, aap apne marks ko add karke total marks se divide kar sakte hain.*

- *Example:* Agar aapke 5 subjects hain aur aapke marks hain: 80, 70, 90, 85, 75
- Total marks obtained: 80 + 70 + 90 + 85 + 75 = 400
- Total marks: 500 (assuming each subject has 100 marks)
- Aggregate: (400 / 500) * 100 = 80%

*Aapke marks card par bhi aggregate mention hota hai, aap wahan se bhi check kar sakte hain.*

*Aapko aur kuch chahiye?*

10/21/25, 2:26â€¯PM - Faizan Kust Cs: Advantages of DBMS:
1.DBMS control Redundancy- duplication/high level freq
+ Having multiple copies 

2.Control Consistent: The values of items must be in proper state
+ If there are mutliple copies of an item than all the copies must have same values

3.Economy of scale: 
+ Scale mean expand

4.Control concurrency:At same time multiple actions performed is called concurrency 
+ When an item is accessed by multiple process at same time
+ Shared data
+ Multiple users
+ Multiple requests

5.Security: DBMs provide security to data by own
+Security is maintained by DBMs internally 
+Management of rights

6.Rapid Application development: If database is already present then we can easily built a new application on the same DB.

7.Backup and Recovery: 
+ Backup:copy of data that is kept safe 

                        LEVELS OF DATA:
1.Real world data : anything exists in a real world
And also have some properties and features.
Example: bank,car

2.Meta Data: Data about data
+ Data that describes data
+ Example: folder properties showing data inside the folder data

3.Data occurrence : 
+ Record about a particular item from the real world
+ Row in a table

11/6/25, 7:52â€¯PM - +92 325 8617855: University of Peshawar and Kohat University Sign MoU to Promote Online Distance Learning

The University of Peshawar and Kohat University of Science and Technology (KUST) have signed a Memorandum of Understanding (MoU) to enhance cooperation in Online Distance Learning (ODL) at the Vice Chancellor's secretariat, University of Peshawar.

The collaboration aims to jointly launch structured online programs to expand access to higher education and promote digital learning across Khyber Pakhtunkhwa.

The MoU was signed by Prof. Dr. Johar Ali, Vice Chancellor of the University of Peshawar, and Prof. Dr. Syed Zafar Ilyas, Vice Chancellor of Kohat University of Science and Technology. 

The ceremony was attended by the Pro Vice Chancellor, University of Peshawar Prof Dr Muhammad Naeem Qazi, Mr. Athar Bangash, Director of Planning and Development at UoP, Prof. Dr. Muhammad Nafees, Director of Online Distance Learning, and Prof. Dr. Zeeshan Bangash from Kohat University, who acted as focal persons.

Prof. Dr. Johar Ali, Vice Chancellor of the University of Peshawar, said: â€œWe want to make higher education accessible for all â€” especially working individuals, homemakers, and those who cannot afford regular programs. Online Distance Learning will help bridge that gap.â€

Prof. Dr. Syed Zafar Ilyas, Vice Chancellor of KUST, remarked: " The initiative reflects the University of Peshawarâ€™s commitment to inclusive and technology-driven education, ensuring that quality learning reaches every corner of society."
